                <tr> 
                 <td width="554" class="grayy">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This is a pleasantly hot sauce, made with tomatoes, red and green bell peppers, garlic, oil, salt and naturally, hot peppers. Among the most traditional recipes, Arrabbiata sauce is loved by those seeking strong and tangy first course dishes. <br> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Bolognese, one of the most popular sauces in Italian gastronomic tradition, is prepared with minced onions, celery and carrots, pork and beef ground meat and tomato pulp.<br> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barilla Olive Sauce is prepared with tomato pulp, minced green and black olives and a few drops of extra virgin olive oil, to bring on your tables all the flavor of an appetizing traditional recipe.<br> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Napoletana sauce, as the name evokes Neapolitan's predilection for good cuisine, and has in tomatoes its most important ingredient. Indeed tomatoes are the basis of many recipes of the Italian culinary tradition and more in general, of Mediterranean one.<br> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Barilla Basil Sauce, a simple yet versatile sauce, probably the first "red" sauce in pasta's history, made from the combination of tomato pulp and fresh basil leaves: an eternal and incomparable aroma. <br></td> 
                 <td width="215" align="center" valign="middle"><img src="../cn/images/cjjs3.jpg" width="200" height="200" class="style"></td>

Pesto alla Genovese Barilla is prepared with the basil expertly blended with pine kernels, pecorino cheese, Grana Padano cheese, etc.<br> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;From more than 100 years of Passion for Pasta, comes Barilla's expertise in sauce, which has the most traditional Mediterranean flavor, and creates delicious dishes with pasta.<br><br> &nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<a href="cpjj-bbyf.asp"><u>To know about Barilla Pasta &amp; Pasta Sauce, Click Here!</u></a></td>

                         <td height="270" align="left" valign="top" class="main"><p align="justify">At Long Home, coffee isn't a drink...it's an experience. Combine the aromas of exotic, in-season coffees from around the world with scrumptious baked goods, unique sandwiches, a relaxed atmosphere and unbeatable Siouxland hospitality and you'll know you've made it home. <br> <br> We hope you'll come by often to visit with friends, meet with colleagues, use the free Wi-Fi or enjoy a little quiet time all to yourself. We'll even decorate it with our signature latte art, a touch not found anywhere else in the area.<br> <br> Long Home Coffee is locally owned and we use many Siouxland suppliers for our specialty items, showcase the work of area artists in our store and actively support our community.</p> <p align="center"><br> <span class="header">Stop by soon or use our convenient drive-thru<br> to have the personalized coffee experience you deserve.</span><br> </p></td>

function FrontPage_Form1_Validator(theForm)
{

  if (theForm.name.value == "")
  {
    alert("Please enter a value for the \"name\" field.");
    theForm.name.focus();
    return (false);
  }

  if (theForm.name.value.length < 5)
  {
    alert("Please enter at least 5 characters in the \"name\" field.");
    theForm.name.focus();
    return (false);
  }

  if (theForm.email.value == "")
  {
    alert("Please enter a value for the \"Valid email address\" field.");
    theForm.email.focus();
    return (false);
  }

  if (theForm.email.value.length < 7)
  {
    alert("Please enter at least 7 characters in the \"Valid email address\" field.");
    theForm.email.focus();
    return (false);
  }

  var checkOK = "ABCDEFGHIJKLMNOPQRSTUVWXYZabcdefghijklmnopqrstuvwxyz0123456789-.-_@";
  var checkStr = theForm.email.value;
  var allValid = true;
  for (i = 0;  i < checkStr.length;  i++)
  {
    ch = checkStr.charAt(i);
    for (j = 0;  j < checkOK.length;  j++)
      if (ch == checkOK.charAt(j))
        break;
    if (j == checkOK.length)
    {
      allValid = false;
      break;
    }
  }
  if (!allValid)
  {
    alert("Please enter only letter, digit and \".-_@\" characters in the \"Valid email address\" field.");
    theForm.email.focus();
    return (false);
  }

  if (theForm.phone.value == "")
  {
    alert("Please enter a value for the \"Phone Number\" field.");
    theForm.phone.focus();
    return (false);
  }

  if (theForm.phone.value.length < 7)
  {
    alert("Please enter at least 7 characters in the \"Phone Number\" field.");
    theForm.phone.focus();
    return (false);
  }

  var checkOK = "0123456789-";
  var checkStr = theForm.phone.value;
  var allValid = true;
  for (i = 0;  i < checkStr.length;  i++)
  {
    ch = checkStr.charAt(i);
    for (j = 0;  j < checkOK.length;  j++)
      if (ch == checkOK.charAt(j))
        break;
    if (j == checkOK.length)
    {
      allValid = false;
      break;
    }
  }
  if (!allValid)
  {
    alert("Please enter only digit characters in the \"Phone Number\" field.");
    theForm.phone.focus();
    return (false);
  }
  return (true);
}

  <meta name="Robots" content="INDEX,FOLLOW">

 <body background="_themes/longrunfishingcharters/webbackground.jpg" bgcolor="#FFFFFF" text="#000000" link="#0000FF" vlink="#FF0000" alink="#336699">
  <!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"> </font>
  <div align="left">
   <font face="Arial"> <!--mstheme--></font>
   <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="border-collapse: collapse" width="864" id="AutoNumber1"> 
    <tbody>
     <tr> 
      <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"><font size="2"> <img border="0" src="Images/WebBanner.jpg" alt="Fishing Charters" width="864" height="72"></font><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
     </tr> 
     <tr> 
      <td bgcolor="#336699" style="border-top: 1px solid #FFFFFF; border-bottom: 1px solid #FFFFFF; padding-left: 4; padding-right: 4; padding-top: 1; padding-bottom: 1" align="center"><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"> <b><font face="Arial" size="2" color="#FFFFFF">Long Run Fishing Charters - NY Fishing Charters - Striped Bass Charters</font></b><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
     </tr> 
     <tr> 
      <td align="center" bgcolor="#FFFFFF"><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"> </font>
       <div align="left">
        <font face="Arial"> <!--mstheme--></font>
        <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="border-collapse: collapse" id="AutoNumber6"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"><a target="_blank" href="http://www.saltwatersportsman.com/"> <img alt="Salt Water Sportsman Magazine - The Fishing Authority Since 1939" hspace="5" src="http://img.timeinc.net/saltwater/Images/sws_logo_450x111.gif" width="450" vspace="10" border="0" height="72"></a><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td align="center" bgcolor="#000000"><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"> <font face="arial, helvetica, sans-serif" color="#ffcc66" size="6"> <b>The Magic Spoon</b></font><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td align="center"><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"><b><font size="2">By John Luchka</font></b><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial">&nbsp;<!--mstheme--></font></td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial">&nbsp;<!--mstheme--></font></td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"><font size="2"><b>Why is this lure the talk of the Northeast? Because it may catch the next world-record striper.</b></font></font>
            <div align="left">
             <font face="Arial"> <!--mstheme--></font>
             <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="border-collapse: collapse" id="AutoNumber7"> 
              <tbody>
               <tr> 
                <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"> <font size="2"> <img src="Images/SWS1.jpg" width="450" height="291"></font><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
               </tr> 
               <tr> 
                <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"> <font size="1"> SPOON FED: A healthy striper that fell for a 12-inch <a title="Bunker Spoon" target="_blank" href="http://www.striperspoons.com/">Secret Spoon</a>. <br> Photo: Gary Caputi </font><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
               </tr> 
              </tbody>
             </table><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"> </font>
            </div><font face="Arial"> <p> <font size="2"> There are few places along the East Coast where striped bass fishing is taken as seriously as it is in Montauk, New York. Good skippers regularly bring in 30-pound stripers, and a 40-pounder doesn't even get a second look at the dock. But lately, Captain Jimmy George's hauls draw a group of rubberneckers every time his boat, the NicoleMarie, returns to the Gone Fishing Marina. </font></p> <!--mstheme--></font>
            <table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="2" width="220" align="right" border="0"> 
             <tbody>
              <tr> 
               <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"><font size="2"> <img src="Images/SWS2.jpg" width="220" height="268"></font><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
              </tr> 
              <tr> 
               <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"><font size="1">HEAVY METAL: Captain Jimmy George proudly displays a 14-inch fluke-pattern spoon. <br> Photo: Nathaniel Welch</font><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
              </tr> 
             </tbody>
            </table><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"> <p><font size="2">In 2004, George landed 95 striped bass weighing more than 40 pounds and eight fish that broke the 50-pound mark. His largest striper that year was a whopping 69 pounds. Last year, during what was by all accounts a slow Montauk striper season, he caught one 50-plus-pound fish and 43 stripers weighing 40 pounds or more. Most impressive of all, these cows were landed on a lure George invented. </font></p> <p><font size="2">George created the lure, a modified bunker spoon he calls the <a title="Bunker Spoon" target="_blank" href="http://www.striperspoons.com/">Secret Spoon</a>, in 2003 for the sole purpose of catching a world-record striper. Drawing on his extensive knowledge of aerodynamics (he's a licensed pilot), George created a large spoon with a fluid action that enticed the big cows to strike. This past fall, a team from SWS hopped aboard the NicoleMarie, a 35-foot Donelle, to see if the <a title="Bunker Spoon" target="_blank" href="http://www.striperspoons.com/">Secret Spoon</a> could live up to the hype it has generated. </font></p> <p><font class="arial, helvetica" color="#003366" size="2"><b> Hard-Wired</b></font></p> <!--mstheme--></font>
            <table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="2" width="220" align="left" border="0"> 
             <tbody>
              <tr> 
               <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"><font size="2"> <img src="Images/SWS3.jpg" width="220" height="264"></font><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
              </tr> 
              <tr> 
               <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"><font size="1">GOOD POINT: Captain George shows off a big bass near the Montauk Lighthouse. <br> Photo: Gary Caputi</font><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
              </tr> 
             </tbody>
            </table><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"> <p><font size="2">Flags snapping on their halyards greeted us when we arrived in Montauk. Not surprisingly, a 20-knot northwest wind kept us at the dock that day, but conditions improved overnight, and we happily tossed the lines the next morning and idled out of Montauk Harbor. As we left the inlet, the NicoleMarie fell in line with the other charter boats as we motored toward famed Montauk Point. </font></p> <p><font size="2">Sitting on the fishbox were two of George's spoons. At 14 inches they looked like dinner platters, save for the pair of welded 10/0 Mustad hooks hanging off the split rings. George explained that with the typical Montauk wire-line lure, an Andrus parachute jig tipped with a porkrind, he caught plenty of fish but not the big stripers that he knew prowled the rips. </font></p> <p><font size="2">"You can't follow the pack if you want to catch really big fish," George said. So in the winter of 2003 he set to work in his garage, hammering out a spoon that was not only oversized but had a seductive swimming motion. </font></p> <p><font size="2">George wanted his spoon to behave like the wing of a plane, catching current instead of wind, and would provide lift and action at a precise speed. As he knocked out version after version, he would take them to a neighbor's pool, break the ice and swim his spoons. </font></p> <p><font size="2">"People started to wonder, 'Who is this crazy guy fishing in a swimming pool in the middle of winter,'" he said. "But I didn't care. I knew I was onto something." </font></p> <p>&nbsp;</p> <!--mstheme--></font>
            <table cellspacing="0" cellpadding="2" width="165" align="right" border="0"> 
             <tbody>
              <tr> 
               <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"><font size="2"> <img src="Images/SWS4.jpg" width="165" height="243"></font><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
              </tr> 
              <tr> 
               <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"><font size="1">CAPTAIN COW: This 69-pound striper fell for a Secret Spoon in 2004.</font><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
              </tr> 
             </tbody>
            </table><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"> <p><font size="2">By adding up to five keel weights and perfecting the angle of the spoon's entire edge, George found an action that he had never seen in a lure. </font></p> <p><font size="2">When pulled at 2 1/2 to three knots, the spoon wobbles naturally while swinging in a six- to 12-foot arc. Depending on their size (there are three models: nine, 12 and 14 inches long) and color, the spoons resemble anything from bunker to fluke. </font> </p> <p><font size="2">The first time George dragged the spoons off Montauk he caught a 44-pounder. The next fish weighed 46 pounds. He had found his lure. But George is the first to admit that just dragging the <a title="Bunker Spoon" target="_blank" href="http://www.striperspoons.com/">Secret Spoon</a> around the ocean won't catch fish. </font> </p> <p><font size="2">"This is a 50-percent lure," George says. "Fifty percent of the success will come from the lure; the other 50 percent from how you fish it." </font></p> <p><font class="arial, helvetica" color="#003366" size="2"><b>Spoon Feeding</b></font></p> </font>
            <div align="left">
             <font face="Arial"> <!--mstheme--></font>
             <table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="border-collapse: collapse" id="AutoNumber8"> 
              <tbody>
               <tr> 
                <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"><font size="2"> <img src="Images/SWS5.jpg" width="450" height="266"></font><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
               </tr> 
               <tr> 
                <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"><font size="1">SPOON BRIGADE: Secret Spoons range in size from 14 inches, left, down to nine inches long. <br> Photo: Nathaniel Welch </font><!--mstheme--></font></td> 
               </tr> 
              </tbody>
             </table><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"> </font>
            </div><font face="Arial"> <p><font size="2">We dropped our spoons in the water off Great Eastern Rip, just as the tide approached what George considers the witching hours. "These spoons work best during the first and last hour and a half of the tide," he says. </font></p> <p><font size="2">At these times, George can work the current to keep the push on his lures at roughly three knots. </font></p> <p><font size="2">The line of charter boats already working the rip had little to report. Most chatter on the radio centered on the slow pick of small fish, but George was unfazed. He fishes his spoons on eight-foot St. Croix trolling rods. His Penn 4/0 and 6/0 reels are spooled with 60-pound Malin wire and marked in 50-foot intervals up to 300 feet. The wire is tied to 20 feet of 150-pound fluorocarbon leader and connected to the spoon via a 200-pound Spro Power swivel. Given the large sweep of water covered by the spoons, only two rods can be fished. And to keep the two lures from fouling on each other, George places the rods in outrodders. (For the record, the IGFA does not recognize fish caught on wire line. The <a title="Bunker Spoon" target="_blank" href="http://www.striperspoons.com/">Secret Spoons</a> can also be trolled with braid.) </font></p> <p><font size="2"> <img src="Images/SWS6.jpg" width="450" height="223"> <br> </font><font size="1">TO THE WIRE: George employs a two-rod trolling spread aboard the NicoleMarie. <br> Illustration: Pete Sucheski </font></p> <p><font size="2">Our spoons found only big bluefish at Great Eastern, and as we started losing the tide George picked up and headed for Block Island to fish the Submarine Channel. As we approached, George explained some of the finer points of dragging the <a title="Bunker Spoon" target="_blank" href="http://www.striperspoons.com/">Secret Spoon</a>. He likes to keep the spoons within five feet of the bottom at all times and often pulls them into a quartering current for best results. </font></p> <p><font size="2">"If you go downtide on a two-knot current, and the boat is traveling at three knots over ground, then the spoons aren't working properly," he says. George also makes sure to drag the spoons by any knoll or bottom irregularity. "That's where the big fish is, and she's not going to move far to eat." </font></p> <p><font size="2">Our lines weren't in the water long before the port rod started bucking. Not long after, we had a 36-pound striper in the boat. </font></p> <p><font size="2">"Now," he says, "let's find a big one." </font> </p> <p><font size="2">George says the <a title="Bunker Spoon" target="_blank" href="http://www.striperspoons.com/">Secret Spoon</a> has seen success up and down the striper coast. Over the winter he had anglers calling from Virginia. One guy called to tell George he was catching so many fish that he extended his vacation by three days, and he needed more spoons delivered by the next day. Another angler from Connecticut called to stock up for spring, fearing he might not be able to get his hands on the spoons come summer. </font></p> <p><font size="2">For sure, the spoons aren't cheap. The nine-inch model sells for $38 (George does not yet sell the two larger models). And it takes some practice and patience to learn how to troll them properly, but no doubt, they will catch big fish. </font> </p> <p><font size="2">"When I'm out by myself, I troll only the 14-inch version," George says. "I might go a few hours without a bite, but when I get one, it's a big fish. I know the world record is swimming off Montauk. It's only a matter of time before we cross paths." </font></p> <p><font size="2"> <img src="Images/SWS7.jpg" width="450" height="299"> <br> </font><font size="1">RIGHT ANGLES: Outrodders are used to keep the spoons from fouling. <br> Photo: Gary Caputi </font> </p></font><p><font face="Arial"><b><font size="2">Saltwater Sportsman Magazine - May 2006</font></b><!--mstheme--></font></p></td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial">&nbsp;<!--mstheme--></font></td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table><!--mstheme--><font face="Arial"> </font>
       </div><font face="Arial"> <!--mstheme--></font></td>

      <td id="content_cell" align="middle" valign="top" width="98%"> 
       <table id="MainContentTable" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" width="100%"> 
        <tbody>
         <tr valign="top"> 
          <td style="PADDING-RIGHT: 20px; PADDING-LEFT: 20px; PADDING-BOTTOM: 15px" valign="top"> 
           <div class="Module HtmlModule"> 
            <div class="Module HtmlModule"> 
             <table class="Panel DesktopModuleTitlePanel" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0" width="100%"> 
              <tbody>
               <tr id="_ctl2__ctl11__ctl0_ct_2136417_2136417_t_tr"> 
                <td id="_ctl2__ctl11__ctl0_ct_2136417_2136417_t_tc" align="left"><br> <h1><span id="_ctl2__ctl11__ctl0_ct_2136417_2136417_t_mt" class="Title">Welcome to Washington</span></h1> </td> 
               </tr> 
               <tr id="_ctl2__ctl11__ctl0_ct_2136417_2136417_t_hr"> 
                <td colspan="2"> 
                 <hr size="1"> </td> 
               </tr> 
              </tbody>
             </table> 
             <table id="_ctl2__ctl11__ctl0_ct_2136417_2136417_Table1" width="100%" cellspacing="0" cellpadding="0"> 
              <tbody>
               <tr valign="top"> 
                <td id="_ctl2__ctl11__ctl0_ct_2136417_2136417_hh">
                 <div> 
                  <table class="NOBORDER" bordercolor="#000000" cellspacing="7" cellpadding="7" align="center" border="0"> 
                   <tbody> 
                    <tr> 
                     <td><font face="Geneva, Arial, Sans-serif" color="#000000" size="2">Washington, state in the Pacific Northwest of the United States. It is bordered by Idaho (E); Oregon, with the Columbia River marking much of the boundary (S); the Pacific Ocean (W); and the Canadian province of British Columbia (N). </font> 
                      <div> 
                       <p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Geneva, Arial, Sans-serif"><font size="2"><strong><em>Area,</em> </strong>68,192 sq mi (176,617 sq km), including 1,483 sq mi (3,841 sq km) of inland water surface. <br><strong><i>Pop.</i> </strong>(2000) 5,894,121, a 21.1% increase since the 1990 census. <br><i><strong>Capital,</strong></i> Olympia. <br><i><strong>Largest city,</strong></i> Seattle.&nbsp;<br><i><strong>Motto,</strong></i> <i>Alki</i> [By and By]. <br><strong><i>State bird,</i> </strong>willow goldfinch. <br><i><strong>State flower,</strong></i> Western rhododendron. <img src="http://venanciogonzalez.point2agent.com/Shared/Cache/HtmlText/54813/Photo/2-Original.img?_Version=631861760084300000" style="WIDTH: 175px; HEIGHT: 112px" alt="" hspace="7" align="right" vspace="32" border="0" sequence="2"><br><i><strong>State tree,</strong></i> Western hemlock. </font></font></p> 
                       <p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Geneva, Arial, Sans-serif" size="2">Much of the land in E Washington is used for dry farming. Irrigation, however, has converted many of the river valleys east of the Cascades (especially the Yakima and Wenatchee) into garden areas. This region contains most of Washington's vineyards; from the 1980s the state has developed an important wine industry. Washington leads the country in the production of apples, sweet cherries, and pears and is a major wheat producer, chiefly in the hilly southeastern Palouse area. Washington is also a major producer of corn, onions, potatoes, apricots, grapes (including those made into wine), and other fruits, nuts, and vegetables. Cattle, dairy goods, sheep, and poultry are also economically important.&nbsp;<img src="http://venanciogonzalez.point2agent.com/Shared/Cache/HtmlText/54813/Photo/1-Original.img?_Version=631861760081500000" style="WIDTH: 112px; HEIGHT: 175px" alt="" hspace="7" align="left" vspace="20" border="0" sequence="1"><br><br>Despite the vast semiarid expanse E of the Cascades, more than half of the state's area is forested, and the lumber and wood-products industry, so important in the early development of the state, remains one of its largest. Many of Washington's cities (among them Tacoma, Bellingham, Everett, and Anacortes) began as sawmill centers. Seattle itself was home to the original Skid Road and lumber, pulp, paper, and related items are still among their major products.&nbsp;<br><br>Other important manufactures in the state are chemicals and primary metals, especially aluminum. Abundant water power and the rich aluminum and magnesium ores found in the Okanogan Highlands in the northeast part of the state have made Washington the nation's leading aluminum producer. <br><br></font><font face="Geneva, Arial, Sans-serif" size="2">Visitors are attracted to Mount Rainier National Park, Olympic National Park, North Cascades National Park, Fort Vancouver and Whitman Mission national historic sites, and Lake Roosevelt National Recreation Area. Mt. Saint Helens&nbsp;, which erupted in 1980, is now a national monument. </font><font face="Arial" size="2"></font></p> 
                       <p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Geneva, Arial, Sans-serif"><font size="2"><span class="other-articles"><em><font size="1"><font face="Geneva, Arial, Sans-serif"></font></font></em></span></font></font>&nbsp;</p> 
                       <p class="MsoNormal"><font face="Geneva, Arial, Sans-serif"><font size="2"><span class="other-articles"><em><font size="1"><font face="Geneva, Arial, Sans-serif">*Columbia Encyclopedia, Sixth Edition, Copyright </font>(c) 2003.</font></em></span></font></font></p>
                      </div></td>
                    </tr>
                   </tbody>
                  </table>
                 </div></td> 
               </tr> 
              </tbody>
             </table> 
            </div> 
           </div> </td> 
         </tr>

       </table> </td>

     <h4>Seaport-E Quality Assurance Program</h4> <strong>Approach:</strong> Long Wave Headquarters in Oklahoma City develops the company's strategic plans and formulates company policy. Long Wave currently has established a Seaport-e placeholder on our publicly available website at www.longwaveinc.com and will populate and manage it for business within 10 days of contract award. The Long Wave Oklahoma City office also performs all contract administration and financial accounting, employee hiring and security processing, under the supervision of the Chief Financial Officer, Jennifer Johnson. Ms. Johnson has been with Long Wave since 1998 and has been the contract administrator for every contract Long Wave has performed. Ms. Johnson serves as Long Wave's single point of contact to the Government Contracting Officer (CO), Contracting Officer's Representatives (CORs) and ordering officials. In the absence of Ms. Johnson, Mr. Phillip Miller (President, Long Wave) acts in behalf of Ms. Johnson for all matters relating to this contract and Long Wave's administration of this contract.
     <br>
     <br> Long Wave assigns a Program Manager to each major program. The program manager assigned responsibility for the Seaport-e Program will be authorized to represent Long Wave in all non-contractual communications with the government. Additionally he is responsible for Long Wave's performance, cost, and schedule on Seaport-e. Mr. Post has 22 years experience as an engineer and managing various DoD programs. Prior to joining Long Wave, Mr. Post was an Associate Technical Fellow at The Boeing Company with work on B-52, F-22, E-6, KC-135 and V-22 platforms. Other duties of the Seaport-e program manager are to direct the program activities of Long Wave employees and our team members: Hi Q, Tryck Nyman Hayes, Hi-Q Inc. and Intuitive Research and Technology Corporation.
     <br>
     <br> <strong>Capability:</strong> Long Wave has experience in managing diverse programs such as maintenance support for TACAMO at Tinker AFB; developing a HF receive system for NAVSEA; and developing specialized software applications to automate use of legacy maintenance data for the US Air Force.
     <br>
     <br> Our program with the broadest scope and most challenging tasks has been the Clarinet Merlin Receive System Program. We designed a set of six receive stations scattered strategically across the globe and a pair of operator terminals. The system is interconnected on the SUBOPAUTHWAN Network. Our implementation of the program required managing two major subcontractors during the development of system control software and highly specialized digital signal processing.
     <br>
     <br> The Clarinet Merlin Receive System (CMRS) is also one tangible example of how Long Wave's innovative technical solutions and management practices have provided significant cost savings to the Navy while facilitating the Navy's conversion to performance based contracting. Long Wave used several technological and programmatic approaches that resulted in an estimate that was 33% of the cost of the USN's reported "should cost". Additionally, all equipment and services were delivered on time and within cost for the estimate proposed by Long Wave. The equipment met or exceeded all requirements of the contract. Long Wave can and will implement performance based approaches to solicitations and orders on the Seaport-e contract. Our existing Indian Head contact and its predecessors have been a model for Navy performance based contracts, and our CMRS project was SPAWAR HQ's first and highly successful attempt at Performance Based Contracting.
     <br>
     <br> We are proud to state that the system design is complete, the system tests have been successful, and all work has either been completed on schedule or is anticipated to complete on time. Our customer, SPAWAR is pleased and hasn't received any unpleasant surprises.
     <br>
     <br> <strong>Managing Change:</strong> Because of Long Wave's business philosophy, managing change, preserving stability, and maintaining technical expertise in the work force has not been an issue. Being a small business, we employ a core staff of talented key people. To augment our staff, Long Wave has made a practice of hiring many individuals who are highly successful professionals and are recently retired from the military, civilian government, and industry. These experts are used as needed for given projects, and are less expensive in terms of overhead than our full-time employees. By drawing on their professional expertise, while minimizing overhead, Long Wave is able to realize cost effectiveness, which we are able to pass on to our customers. We compliment this approach by implementing a mentor/trainee program to groom junior level technicians and program personnel to develop their skills while keeping our rates competitive.
     <br>
     <br> As we provide these "Baby Boomers" with a stable dedicated work force, and time advances through the remainder of the "Baby Boomer" generation's retirement cycle, we anticipate a continuation of our successful hiring practices.
     <br>
     <br> Additionally, as the new Seaport-e programs replace previous support programs, Long Wave desires to interview and hire key individuals who are being displaced as their programs are being terminated.
     <br>
     <br> For other professional placement, Long Wave employs the use of dedicated in-house recruiters from our Oklahoma City and Ft. Worth offices, who specialize in recruiting qualified, professional employees to fill any requirement. Through our extensive network of recruiters, Long Wave is readily equipped to supply quality professionals in a timely manner to task orders for Virtual SYSCOM, institute best practices throughout and realize cost savings. This arrangement allows Long Wave to offer a low overhead rate while providing timely, cost effective and quality professional and administrative support services to the Navy.
     <br>
     <br> <strong>Monitoring and Maximizing Quality:</strong> It is Long Wave's philosophy that our quality program starts when we write a proposal and finishes when the contract is completed.
     <br>
     <br> By doing a thorough system engineering analysis, creating functional models and allocating requirements to hardware and software, a quality design is initiated. By creating accurate documentation, controlling changes, performing inclusive testing, and empowering employees to demand quality, we work towards maximizing quality.
     <br>
     <br> The Long Wave Quality Assurance Program is built upon an overall methodology that provides to all concerned the necessary evidence needed to establish confidence that the quality function is being performed. This program is implemented on any government contract that requires a QA Program.
     <br>
     <br> Long Wave and/or our teammates will prepare a Quality Assurance plan structured around the scope of each task order. Each plan will be approved by Long Wave management and submitted to the government 90 days after the receipt of the task order.
     <br>
     <br> <strong>Guaranteeing Responsiveness and Cooperation:</strong> It is Long Wave's policy to be open, honest, and straight forward with our customers. Responsiveness has been a benchmark of our performance with contracting on Navy IDIQ efforts accomplished in days rather than weeks. We guarantee responsiveness and cooperation for personnel and service efforts by addressing these issues in employee annual merit reviews. Our ability to rapidly respond to customer requests for everything from software development to personnel staffing to engineering analysis has made us the "contractor of choice" for our Navy and other customers.
     <br>
     <br> <strong>Problem Resolution:</strong> Long Wave's approach to problem resolution will be to document and publish an "Issue Log" prior to issues becoming problems. The log will be kept current, on a weekly basis, and will be routed to Long Wave's management weekly as well as to the customer's program management office monthly or more frequently if needed. Working together, Long Wave's program manager and the customer's program office will jointly assign issues to appropriate individuals. Each issue will be assigned a specific resolution date. Issues will be subsequently tracked and cleared. If not clearable work around solutions will be worked out with customer approval. 
     <br>
     <br> 
     <div style="color:#999999; border-top:dotted 1px #999999;">
       Need more information or have a question for Long Wave?
      <br> Contact us via <a href="contact_info.aspx">our website</a> or by phone at 405.235.2217. 
     </div>
